## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through restoring forces, damping, and driving terms. The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force (powers of x), damping (velocity-dependent), or parametric/external driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-cubic nonlinearity)
- Quintic Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Damped pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (sinusoidal restoring + damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping + cubic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 (mixed nonlinearities)
- Softening spring with drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (driven with sine)
- General polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric restoring force)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ‚Üí Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ‚Üí Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ‚Üí Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ‚Üí Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ‚Üí Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x¬≥, x‚Åµ) preserve symmetry of oscillation; even powers (x¬≤) break symmetry ‚Äî check if the system has symmetric or asymmetric behavior
- Velocity-position coupling terms like x¬≤v indicate amplitude-dependent damping (Van der Pol type self-excitation or limit cycles)
- If time t appears only inside trigonometric functions, the system is periodically driven; the driving frequency is a key parameter to identify
- Cubic restoring force x¬≥ with same/opposite sign as linear term x indicates hardening/softening spring behavior respectively
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy analysis (conservative or dissipative) constrains the functional form
- Sinusoidal position dependence sin(c*x) suggests a periodic potential (e.g., pendulum), distinguishable from polynomial restoring forces by large-amplitude behavior
- Velocity terms with odd powers (v, v¬≥) represent dissipative forces; even powers of v multiplied by v (e.g., v*|v|) represent quadratic drag
- If phase-space trajectories show limit cycles, expect balanced nonlinear damping terms like (1 - x¬≤)*v that provide negative damping at small amplitudes and positive damping at large amplitudes
